Factory 053 - Audit Report
Factory Profile: factory recovering from recent fire incident, under special monitoring by local authorities
============================================================

[Forced Labor]
**Audit Finding Ref:** FL-053-003 **| Compliance Area:** Forced Labor (ILO Core Convention 29) **| Audit Date:** October 26, 2023

**Background & Context:** Following the major fire incident on August 12, 2023, which resulted in significant damage to the western sewing module, the audit scope included a heightened review of worker status and freedom of movement to assess potential vulnerabilities during the recovery period, particularly given the factory's placement under special monitoring by district authorities. Inspector observations on the factory compound noted the continued presence of dormitory facilities, which house approximately 60% of the workforce, and a review of security gate logs from September 1 to October 20 indicated a pattern wherein the identities of workers exiting the premises after shift hours were routinely recorded by guard personnel. During confidential interviews conducted with 17 dormitory-resident workers on October 26, four individuals from the fabric cutting department separately reported that their national identity cards had been retained by factory management since the fire, citing "administrative processing for safety re-registration," a practice which they stated inhibited their ability to seek alternative employment. While management provided documentation of the card retention for purported payroll and government reporting updates, the unilateral withholding of these original personal documents, combined with the documented exit controls, effectively restricts workers’ ability to voluntarily terminate employment, constituting a retention of workers under duress.

**Severity: Critical**

**Follow-up Note:** Corrective Action Plan (CAP) must address immediate return of original identity documents, revision of security protocols, and implementation of a documented policy affirming voluntary employment.

[Child Labor]
During a review of human resources documentation and subsequent floor observations on November 14, 2023, a compliance check regarding minimum age was initiated following the factory's re-hiring process after the October fire incident. While all 12 personnel files reviewed for workers hired post-incident contained valid identification verifying age above 18, an interview with three production workers from the cutting section revealed a discrepancy. Worker A-053-12 (name confidential) stated during a private interview on November 15 that a younger individual, estimated to be 15 or 16 years of age and introduced as a worker's relative, had been informally assisting with bundling tasks on the factory floor for two hours daily over the past week to support family income, a fact corroborated by a second worker interview. This constitutes a breach of CLA-01 (Child Labor Prevention) as the presence of a minor in a production area, regardless of formal employment status, violates the zero-tolerance protocol, especially under the factory's current heightened monitoring conditions. The management was immediately notified and stated the individual was not on payroll and would be prohibited from entering the production area henceforth; however, the lack of formal gatekeeping controls and visitor logs for the temporary facility was noted as a systemic failure. **Severity: Critical**.

[Emergency Preparedness]
**Audit Finding REF: EP-2023-053-04**

**Area:** Emergency Preparedness
**Date of Inspection:** October 26, 2023
**Background & Context:** Following the significant fire incident on August 15, 2023, and the subsequent placement of the factory under special monitoring by the Liangzhou District Fire Authority, this audit focused on evaluating the restoration and operational status of emergency protocols. Special attention was paid to the implementation of the corrective action plan submitted to authorities in September 2023.

**Observations & Interviews:** While management has reinstated fire extinguishers and repaired exit signage in the main production hall, the audit team noted a critical lapse in procedural readiness. A surprise evacuation drill was requested at 10:30 AM on the audit date; the drill execution was chaotic, with evacuation time for the 427 personnel on shift clocked at 9 minutes and 47 seconds, exceeding the maximum permitted 4 minutes for a facility of this layout. Furthermore, interviews with 7 workers from the cutting and sewing departments revealed that post-incident emergency training has been minimal and ad-hoc. Three workers were unaware of the new assembly point location established after the August fire, and the designated floor wardens could not produce the updated headcount checklists for their sections.

**Conclusion & Follow-up:** The factory has made tangible progress in restoring physical emergency equipment. However, the failure to conduct effective, regular drills and to adequately train all workers on revised evacuation procedures post-incident has resulted in a system that is not functionally prepared for an emergency, directly contravening section 7.4 of the Corporate Code of Conduct and local fire regulations under the special monitoring order. This represents a severe and immediate risk to worker safety.
**Severity: Critical**

[Harassment & Abuse]
**Audit Finding Ref:** SA-053-HA-024
**Compliance Area:** Harassment & Abuse (SA8000: 3.1 / Buyer Code: Sec. 8.2)
**Date of Assessment:** October 26, 2023
**Background & Context:** Following the fire incident of August 2023, which resulted in the destruction of the primary sewing hall, Factory 053 has been operating under a partial production schedule with a reduced workforce of approximately 60% while reconstruction is underway. This period of operational stress and management transition has been noted as a potential risk factor for workplace conduct.
**Observations & Interviews:** During the review of policies and procedures, the Harassment Prevention Policy was found to be adequately documented and posted. However, confidential interviews conducted on October 26 with 14 production line workers (approximately 18% of the current workforce) revealed a pattern of concerning behavior. Multiple workers from the temporary packing section reported instances of verbal abuse and intimidation by a specific line supervisor, referred to as "Supervisor Chen," who has been reassigned from the damaged section. These reports, corroborated across three separate interviews, indicated the supervisor used derogatory language and threats of termination related to productivity pressures during the recovery period. The interviewed workers expressed a fear of retaliation, with none having utilized the formal grievance mechanism due to this concern.
**Analysis:** While a policy framework exists, the failure of management to ensure its practical application and to foster an environment where workers can report without fear constitutes a violation. The behavior described meets the definition of verbal abuse and psychological coercion. The current vulnerable state of the workforce post-incident exacerbates the severity of this failure to protect worker dignity.
**Follow-up Note:** Management must be immediately notified to intervene, and a re-training session for all supervisory staff on the harassment policy is required, with evidence of disciplinary action for the implicated individual to be verified.
**Severity: Moderate**

[Working Hours & Overtime]
**Audit Finding Reference:** WH-OT-2024-053-02
**Compliance Area:** Working Hours & Overtime (BSCI Code: 6, ILO Convention 1)
**Background & Context:** Following the fire incident on 12 March 2024 and the factory's subsequent placement under special monitoring by the local Labor Department, particular attention was paid to working hour practices during the audit conducted on 15-17 April 2024. Management stated that recovery operations and backlog fulfillment had placed significant pressure on production schedules.

**Inspector Observations & Worker Interviews:** A review of payroll records for March and April 2024 revealed a consistent pattern of extended overtime. For the pay period ending 5 April 2024, approximately 78% of the 312 production line workers exceeded the 60-hour workweek limit stipulated by national law, with an average of 67 hours logged. During confidential interviews with 14 workers from the cutting and sewing departments, 12 confirmed working 12-hour shifts, 7 days per week, since the resumption of operations on 25 March. While the factory has maintained accurate overtime premium payment, the excessive hours present a significant worker fatigue risk, especially pertinent given the recent emergency and the need for heightened safety vigilance.

**Conclusion:** The factory is in violation of statutory limits on maximum working hours. This is considered a systemic failure, exacerbated by the recovery period, and requires immediate corrective action to schedule production within legal parameters.
**Severity: Critical**
**Follow-up Note:** The local authorities have been notified of this finding as per special monitoring protocol; a corrective action plan must be submitted to the audit team within 7 business days.

[Contracts & Human Resources]
**Audit Finding Ref: C-HR-053-24-008**
**Compliance Area:** Contracts & Human Resources
**Background & Context:** Following the fire incident on 12 March 2024 and the subsequent placement of the facility under special monitoring by the district labour office, this audit included a heightened review of employment documentation and post-incident human resources procedures to ensure stability and compliance during the recovery period.
**Observations & Interviews:** A document review of personnel files for 30 workers rehired post-fire (selected from a stratified sample of 120) conducted on 23 April 2024 revealed that 18 files contained only a basic workshop attendance registration form lacking essential terms of employment, contrary to national labour law Article 24. Interviews with 7 of the affected workers from the cutting and finishing departments confirmed they had not been provided with any written contract outlining their wages, working hours, or job description since returning to work, creating significant ambiguity regarding their terms of employment. Furthermore, management acknowledged a procedural backlog in formalizing contracts due to "administrative pressures during reconstruction."
**Conclusion & Follow-up:** The failure to issue legally compliant written employment contracts to a substantial portion of the rehired workforce constitutes a breach of fundamental worker rights and undermines the stability intended by the post-fire monitoring program. The factory is required to regularize all employment contracts and provide copies to workers, with evidence submitted to the auditor within 30 days.
**Severity: Moderate**

[Discrimination]
**Audit Reference:** SA-8.1 / EEO-2023-053-D
**Finding Background:** In light of the factory's operational restructuring following the fire incident of 15 April 2023, and the subsequent hiring of approximately 120 new production staff, a focused review of recruitment and employment practices was conducted to ensure alignment with the Supplier Code of Conduct’s non-discrimination clauses. This area is of heightened concern during recovery phases to prevent exploitative practices.
**Observations & Interviews:** A review of personnel files for 45 workers hired between 1 May and 30 June 2023 revealed a consistent pattern where all 28 sewing operator positions were filled by female candidates, while all 17 warehousing and maintenance roles were filled by male candidates. During worker interviews conducted on 26 July 2023, four female workers separately indicated they had inquired about higher-paying machine technician vacancies but were informed by the hiring supervisor, Mr. Chen, that "those jobs are not suitable for women" and were instead directed to apply for sewing roles. The factory's posted job advertisements did not specify gender requirements.
**Conclusion:** This constitutes a clear pattern of gender-based discrimination in hiring and job assignment, directly contravening section 3.4 of the Code of Conduct. The practice systematically limits career advancement and earning potential for female workers.
**Severity: Moderate**
**Follow-up Note:** Management has been instructed to provide documented evidence of revised hiring protocols and non-discrimination training for all HR personnel by the next follow-up inspection.

[Occupational Safety & Health]
**Audit Finding Ref:** OSH-053-2023-08
**Compliance Area:** Occupational Safety & Health
**Date of On-Site Verification:** October 26, 2023

Following the major fire incident in July 2023, which resulted in the temporary closure of the sewing wing, the audit team focused a significant portion of the inspection on fire safety protocols and emergency preparedness. While the management has made visible efforts to repair structural damage, observations on the date of inspection revealed that the primary emergency exit in the newly reopened cutting department (Exit B, West Wall) was found to be partially obstructed by three bales of incoming fabric, reducing the clear width to approximately 0.7 meters. Furthermore, interviews conducted with 7 workers from that department indicated that the monthly fire drill scheduled for October had not been conducted, with several workers confirming they were unaware of the updated assembly point location post-renovation. This constitutes a failure to maintain clear egress paths and provide regular emergency training as required by local ordinance 12.4.5 and the factory's own post-incident action plan submitted to authorities. Given the factory's status under special monitoring and the recent history of a serious fire, this lapse in maintaining fundamental fire safety measures is of particular concern.
**Severity: Moderate**
**Follow-up Note:** Corrective Action Plan (CAP) required within 7 days, with photographic evidence of cleared egress to be submitted to the audit team.

[Freedom of Association & Collective Bargaining]
**Audit Finding Ref: FA-053-24-008 | Compliance Area: Freedom of Association & Collective Bargaining (Code: FOA.01)**

Following the fire incident of 15 March 2024 and the subsequent special monitoring regime enacted by local authorities, this audit included a focused review of industrial relations practices. While management presented documentation of a legally registered trade union, interviews conducted on 22 April 2024 with 14 workers from various production departments revealed a consistent narrative of union activity being actively discouraged. Specifically, three workers separately reported (notes on file: WI-053-22 to WI-053-24) that supervisory staff had implied that union membership could jeopardize future employment opportunities, particularly during this fragile recovery period, stating "it is not the time for division." Furthermore, a review of meeting minutes for the past six months showed no evidence of good faith bargaining between union representatives and management on post-fire working conditions, despite worker concerns submitted in January. This constitutes a failure to uphold the principles of freedom of association and collective bargaining, as the environment suppresses the workers' right to organize freely.
**Severity: Moderate**
**Follow-up:** Required corrective action plan to include management training and a formal, documented bargaining process.

[Wages & Benefits]
**Audit Finding Reference:** WAG-SC-2024-053-02
**Compliance Area:** Wages & Benefits (SCSA Standard 8.1, 8.2)
**Date of Discovery:** 17 April 2024

During the review of wage records for the post-recovery operational period of February to March 2024, following the fire incident of 15 January, a discrepancy was identified between the production output records and the wages paid for piece-rate workers in the sewing section. Inspector observations of daily output sheets, cross-referenced with signed pay slips for the pay period ending 28 March, indicated that 34 of 87 piece-rate workers received less than the local minimum monthly wage requirement. Subsequent confidential interviews with 12 affected workers on 18 April confirmed that their compensation for March, while reflecting accurate piece counts, did not meet the statutory floor, with one worker providing a payslip showing a net payment of CNY 1,980 against a mandated minimum of CNY 2,190. This constitutes a failure to guarantee minimum wage, a core violation, despite the factory's cited financial pressures during reconstruction. Management acknowledged the oversight, attributing it to an administrative error in the new payroll system implemented post-fire. A corrective action plan is required. Severity: Critical.


============================================================
Factory 054 - Audit Report
Factory Profile: small family-owned factory with 50-100 workers, limited HR capacity, first time being audited
============================================================

[Wages & Benefits]
Audit Code: WB-003-F054
During the review of payroll records for the period of January to March 2024, it was observed that the factory utilizes a complex piece-rate system for sewing operators, which was not clearly articulated in the employment contracts or posted for worker understanding. Interviews conducted on 2024-04-15 with a sample of 8 production line workers revealed a universal lack of comprehension regarding how their individual piece rates translate to their final monthly wage, and none could verify the accuracy of their pay against their own production output. Furthermore, payroll register inspection identified that for 12 workers across two pay periods in February, the calculated piece-rate earnings fell below the local statutory minimum wage, with the shortfall being made up via an opaque "attendance bonus." This failure to ensure all workers receive at least the legal minimum wage for all hours worked, and the lack of transparent wage calculation, constitutes a violation of local labor law and brand Code of Conduct section 7.2. The factory's limited HR capacity and lack of prior audit experience are noted as contributing factors, but do not excuse the violation. A follow-up note is required to obtain a full reconciliation of all worker wages for the last 12 months to ascertain the full scope of non-compliance.
Severity: Critical

[Occupational Safety & Health]
**Compliance Area:** A07 Occupational Safety & Health (OSH)
**Reference:** Finding-OSH-054-01
**Date of Inspection:** 23 October 2023
**Context:** The inspection of the OSH environment focused on the main production floor, storage areas, and emergency preparedness protocols. The factory, being a first-time auditee, demonstrated a basic awareness of safety requirements but lacked formalized systems and documented procedures. Inspector observations on the date of the inspection, corroborated by interviews with 8 production workers conducted on 24 October 2023, identified a persistent failure to ensure clear and unobstructed access to emergency exits and firefighting equipment. Specifically, the primary fire exit in the eastern cutting section was partially blocked by three rolls of stored fabric and a mobile cart, reducing the effective egress width to approximately 0.6 meters, which is below the minimum regulatory requirement of 1.1 meters. Furthermore, two fire extinguishers (ID: FE-12 & FE-15) located in the packing area had inspection tags that were last updated in December 2022, indicating they have not undergone the required annual maintenance check. Worker interviews confirmed that emergency evacuation drills have never been conducted, and several newer employees were unsure of the location of all exits. This constitutes a significant and immediate risk to worker safety in the event of a fire or other emergency. **Severity: Critical**

[Emergency Preparedness]
**Audit Finding Reference: EP-2023-054-02**

**Background/Context:** The audit scope included a review of emergency preparedness protocols and physical provisions in alignment with section 7.1 of the Client's Code of Conduct. Factory management indicated during the opening meeting that general fire extinguishers are present and that workers are given verbal instructions upon hire. The factory layout comprises a single main production hall on the ground floor with one primary exit and a secondary emergency exit at the rear leading to a secured alleyway.

**Observations & Evidence:** During the physical inspection on 12 October 2023, the audit team verified the presence of six 9kg ABC-type fire extinguishers, all with current service tags. However, the primary evacuation route along the western wall was partially obstructed by three rolls of stored fabric and a cutting table, reducing the clear egress width to approximately 0.7 meters. The secondary emergency exit door, while unlocked during the audit, was found to be fitted with a deadbolt lock requiring a key from the inside; the key was not observed in the designated break-glass box, which was empty. Furthermore, no illuminated exit signs were installed, and the factory lacks a documented emergency action plan or evacuation diagrams. Interviews conducted with a cross-section of 8 production workers on the same date revealed significant confusion; 7 workers were unaware of the secondary exit's location, and all interviewed stated that no emergency drill had ever been conducted in their tenure, which for some exceeded three years.

**Conclusion & Follow-Up Requirement:** The factory has failed to establish and maintain basic elements of an emergency action and fire prevention plan, as evidenced by blocked egress, a locked exit without immediate means of egress, lack of worker training, and the absence of emergency drills. This constitutes a failure to provide for the fundamental safety of personnel. The factory management is required to submit a corrective action plan addressing these systemic gaps within 14 calendar days.

**Severity: Moderate**

[Harassment & Abuse]
**Audit Finding Ref: FA-054-2023-SA.07**  
During the inspection conducted on 17-18 October 2023, the audit scope included a review of policies and procedures related to the prevention of harassment and abuse in the workplace. It was noted that while the factory management expressed a general commitment to a respectful environment, there was no formal written policy against harassment and abuse, nor was there evidence of a functional grievance mechanism communicated to workers. In interviews with 12 production workers (approximately 15% of the workforce), 3 workers anonymously reported instances of verbal abuse and intimidation by a line supervisor, describing being shouted at and threatened with dismissal for minor performance errors; however, no formal complaints had been lodged due to fear of retaliation and lack of known reporting channels. The absence of a defined policy and procedural safeguards, coupled with credible interview testimony indicating a pattern of intimidating conduct, constitutes a failure to ensure a workplace free from abuse. **Severity: Moderate** - A corrective action plan is required, including policy development, supervisor training, and the establishment of a confidential reporting procedure.

[Discrimination]
**Audit Finding Reference:** SA-054-2023-07 / Discrimination (Code: HR-D.01)
**Date of Inspection:** October 26, 2023

During the review of human resources management systems, it was noted that the factory, being a first-time auditee with a family-owned operational structure, lacks formal written policies prohibiting discrimination in hiring, remuneration, promotion, and access to training. Investigator observations and cross-referenced payroll records from Q3 2023 indicated a workforce composition exclusively comprising individuals from the same regional ethnicity and speaking the local dialect. Subsequent confidential interviews, conducted with 12 workers on the aforementioned date, revealed consistent anecdotal accounts that managerial positions are exclusively held by male members of the owning family, with no female employees in supervisory roles. While no active grievances regarding discriminatory harassment were presented, the absence of procedural safeguards and the demonstrable lack of diversity in leadership constitute a systemic failure to establish a workplace free from discrimination, requiring immediate procedural correction. **Severity: Moderate**


============================================================
Factory 055 - Audit Report
Factory Profile: newly established factory with 100-200 workers, young workforce, still building compliance systems
============================================================

[Wages & Benefits]
**Compliance Area: Wages & Benefits (Audit Code: WB)**
**Reference: FG-055-2024-03-14-WB01**

A review of payroll records for the period of January 1, 2024, to March 14, 2024, alongside worker interviews conducted on March 13, 2024, indicates systemic non-compliance regarding the calculation and payment of overtime premiums. Inspectors noted that while the base hourly wage for production workers meets the local minimum wage requirement, the factory's payroll system applies a flat rate for all hours worked, failing to distinguish between regular and overtime hours as mandated by national labor law Article 24. This was corroborated in confidential interviews with 12 of 18 randomly selected line workers, who confirmed receiving the same hourly rate for workweeks exceeding 60 hours, including on weekends. The factory management acknowledged this is a legacy practice from their initial operational phase and that their new HR software, scheduled for implementation in Q2, is intended to rectify the calculation methodology. Consequently, all overtime hours worked have been compensated at the regular rate, resulting in a significant underpayment to a majority of the workforce. **Severity: Critical**

[Occupational Safety & Health]
**Audit Finding Reference:** OSH-2024-055-03
**Area of Compliance:** Occupational Safety & Health
**Date of Inspection:** 17 May 2024

**Finding Detail:** During the walk-through of the production floor and warehouse on the aforementioned date, the audit team observed a systemic lack of standardized Lockout/Tagout (LOTO) procedures for machinery maintenance and cleaning. Specifically, four sewing machine power isolation points and the main electrical panel serving the cutting section were found to be without any physical locking devices or warning tags, posing a risk of accidental energization. This observation was corroborated during confidential worker interviews conducted on 16 May 2024, where 3 out of 8 interviewed machine operators from Section B stated they were not formally trained on or provided with equipment to safely isolate machines before clearing jams or performing basic cleaning. While management acknowledges this gap and attributes it to the nascent stage of their safety program development, the absence of controlled energy isolation protocols presents a clear and present danger of serious injury. A follow-up note indicates that the factory's provided Corrective Action Plan (CAP) references the procurement of LOTO kits by the end of Q3 2024, which is deemed an acceptable timeline given the finding's context.
**Severity: Moderate**

[Contracts & Human Resources]
**Audit Finding Ref: HR-055-03**
**Compliance Area: Contracts & Human Resources**
**Date of Discovery: October 26, 2023**

During the review of human resources documentation and subsequent worker interviews, a systemic non-conformance was identified regarding the implementation of legally binding employment contracts. The audit team, having reviewed a sample of 25 personnel files selected from workers hired throughout the past eight months, observed that only 7 files contained a signed, individualized employment contract specifying essential terms such as wage rates, job description, and working hours, representing a coverage rate of just 28%. Interviews conducted with 18 production workers on the audit date revealed a consistent lack of awareness; 15 interviewees confirmed they had signed only an attendance register or a brief onboarding form upon hiring, with no copy of any contractual document provided for their retention. This absence of formalized contracts constitutes a failure to establish the fundamental employer-employee relationship in accordance with local labor law, leaving workers without clear, written proof of their agreed terms and conditions of employment, which is particularly concerning given the factory's nascent stage of development and its largely inexperienced workforce. The management representative acknowledged the gap, attributing it to rapid scaling and an underdeveloped HR department, but offered no immediate corrective evidence.
**Severity: Moderate**

[Harassment & Abuse]
**Compliance Area 3.1: Harassment & Abuse (Audit Code: HR-08)**
A review of the factory's human resources management systems, conducted on 12 March 2024, found that while a general policy statement prohibiting harassment exists within the employee handbook, the implementation of a functional grievance mechanism and systematic training for supervisory staff remains under development. During confidential interviews with 18 production workers, approximately one-third (6 workers) from the cutting and sewing departments reported experiencing or witnessing derogatory comments and verbal intimidation from line leaders, particularly during peak production periods, with one interviewee stating, "The supervisors shout and call us slow and useless to meet the targets, but we do not know where to complain without fear." This is corroborated by the absence of any recorded harassment-related grievances or investigation reports for the period since operations began in Q3 2023, indicating a lack of a trusted and accessible reporting channel. Given the young demographic of the workforce and the nascent state of the compliance infrastructure, the absence of a clearly communicated, confidential procedure, coupled with credible interview testimony, constitutes a failure to ensure a workplace free from abusive practices.
**Severity: Moderate**
*Follow-up Note: Management has committed to developing a formal anti-harassment policy and procedure (Ref: CAP-055-12) by 30 April 2024.*

[Forced Labor]
**Audit Finding Ref: FL-2023-055-02**

During the review of payroll records for the period covering March through May 2023, and subsequent confidential worker interviews conducted on 12 May 2023, it was noted that the factory's practice regarding worker mobility presents a significant compliance risk. Management confirmed, and worker interviews with 8 of 15 randomly selected production staff corroborated, that original national identity cards are systematically retained by the factory's security department upon worker hire, under the stated rationale of "safekeeping and processing." This practice was observed to be a uniform administrative policy, depriving workers of control over their own legal identity documents. This retention effectively restricts their freedom of movement and ability to terminate employment at will, creating a situation of undue coercion and constituting a violation of the Forced Labor and Involuntary Servitude standard (Code: FL.3). A corrective action plan must address the immediate return of all original documents and the implementation of a lawful verification and copy-retention policy. **Severity: Critical**

[Emergency Preparedness]
**Audit Finding EP-03: Emergency Preparedness & Fire Safety Drill Documentation**
**Background & Observation:** During the inspection conducted on 12 March 2024, the audit team reviewed the factory's emergency preparedness protocols, with a specific focus on the execution and documentation of required evacuation drills. As a newly established facility with a workforce reported to be between 100-200 predominantly young employees, the implementation of robust and regularly practiced emergency procedures is of particular importance. The management representative presented a draft emergency action plan; however, no verifiable records of a full-site evacuation drill conducted within the last calendar year could be produced. This was corroborated during confidential worker interviews on the same date, wherein 8 out of 12 randomly selected workers from various departments stated they had never participated in a formal drill since their hiring, and the remaining 4 described only informal departmental walkthroughs without alarm activation or timed egress.

**Finding:** The factory has failed to conduct, document, and maintain records of mandatory semi-annual full-site emergency evacuation drills, as required by section 7.2 of the Responsible Sourcing Code of Conduct. The absence of practiced drills for a workforce unfamiliar with established evacuation routes and assembly points presents a significant risk to worker safety in the event of a real emergency. The audit team notes that while the physical egress paths were found to be generally unobstructed, procedural preparedness cannot be assumed without demonstrated practice.

**Follow-up Action Required:** Factory management must develop and implement a schedule for immediate corrective action, including the completion of a documented full-site drill with worker participation and timing metrics, to be submitted for review by 26 April 2024.
**Severity: Moderate**


============================================================
Factory 056 - Audit Report
Factory Profile: factory with history of compliance issues, under corrective action plan from previous audit
============================================================

[Forced Labor]
**Audit Finding Ref: FL-056-03-2024**

Regarding the compliance area of Forced Labor, a review of worker recruitment and employment practices was conducted on March 12-14, 2024. This review was of particular focus given the factory’s existing Corrective Action Plan (CAP-FL-056-09-2023) stemming from previous findings related to retention of personal documents. During this assessment, it was verified that the factory has ceased the practice of holding original identity documents; however, interviews with 17 newly hired migrant workers from the stitching section revealed a persistent and concerning pattern. These workers reported paying recruitment fees equivalent to approximately one month's gross wages to third-party agents for their employment, fees which are being repaid through monthly deductions from their paychecks as observed in reviewed payslips. The factory's management acknowledged awareness of these arrangements but stated they are not party to the contracts, failing to provide due diligence documentation demonstrating action to prevent such debt bondage. This constitutes a failure to effectively implement the remediation required under the previous CAP and creates a situation of coercion through indebtedness.

**Severity: Moderate**

[Discrimination]
**Audit Finding Ref:** 056-SOC-03-24
**Compliance Area:** Discrimination (Aligned with Standards SA8000:2014, Section 5 & relevant local labor ordinances)
**Date of On-site Verification:** March 12, 2024
**Background & Context:** Factory 056 is currently operating under an approved Corrective Action Plan (CAP) following the non-conformances identified in the audit of November 2023 (Report 056-F-11-23), which included issues related to unfair disciplinary practices. The current audit included a review of hiring, promotion, and disciplinary records from January 1, 2024, to the audit date, alongside confidential worker interviews.

**Inspector Observations & Worker Interview Notes:** A review of promotion records for the first quarter of 2024 revealed a pattern wherein all eight (8) supervisory promotions within the sewing department were awarded to male employees, despite approximately 65% of the sewing operators being female. During confidential interviews conducted on March 12, 2024, with a stratified sample of 22 workers (12 female, 10 male), multiple female workers expressed the perception that management favors men for "leadership roles," with one worker stating, "They tell us women are less able to handle the pressure and machine breakdowns." This sentiment was not evident in other departments. Management could not provide documented, objective criteria for the promotion decisions in question, citing "management discretion" and "seniority," though seniority lists did not support this claim for at least three of the promoted individuals.

**Analysis & Conclusion:** The evidence indicates a practice of gender-based discrimination in promotion opportunities within a specific department, which violates both the factory's own published code of conduct and internationally recognized social accountability standards. This finding represents a continuation of the fundamental fairness issues noted in the previous audit and suggests inadequate implementation of the related CAP element. **Severity: Moderate**

[Freedom of Association & Collective Bargaining]
**Audit Reference:** FO-056-24-008 | **Compliance Area:** FOA & CB (CLS-04) | **Date of On-site Inspection:** 2024-10-17

**Background & Context:** Factory 056 remains under a Corrective Action Plan (CAP) stemming from the Q3 2023 audit, which identified systemic shortcomings in fostering an environment conducive to freedom of association. The current inspection, including a review of documentation and confidential worker interviews, focused on verifying implementation of the agreed-upon remedial measures, specifically the establishment of a functional and democratically elected Worker Representative Committee (WRC) as per CAP milestone dated 2024-06-30.

**Observations & Findings:** Review of meeting minutes and payroll records revealed that the formally constituted WRC has not convened in the preceding three (3) months, contravening its own charter mandating monthly sessions. During confidential interviews held on 2024-10-17, 7 out of 12 randomly selected workers from the sewing and finishing departments stated they were unaware of the current WRC member identities or the established grievance channel, indicating a failure in communication and representative function. Furthermore, interview notes from two (2) separate WRC members, conducted privately, revealed management had unilaterally postponed the last two scheduled meetings due to production targets without consulting the committee, thereby obstructing its operational autonomy.

**Conclusion:** The evidence demonstrates a regression from previous commitments and a failure to sustain the corrective actions, resulting in a de facto non-functioning representative body that inhibits the right to collective representation. This constitutes a repeated violation of the agreed CAP and benchmark CLS-04.01.
**Severity: Moderate**

[Harassment & Abuse]
**Audit Finding Ref:** SSA-056-2023-09.2.1
**Compliance Area:** Harassment & Abuse (CC: 9.2)
**Background & Context:** Following a previous audit in Q4 2022 (Audit Ref: SSA-056-2022-11), which identified systemic failures in management-worker communication and a lack of documented grievance procedures for harassment, Factory 056 was placed under a Corrective Action Plan (CAP) requiring, among other items, the implementation of a formal, worker-understood policy against harassment and abuse, and verified training for all supervisory staff by March 31, 2023.
**Inspector Observations & Worker Interviews:** During the current audit visit on September 18-19, 2023, while a revised policy document was on file, verification of training completion records showed only 40% of line supervisors and 0% of middle management had attended the mandated sessions. Furthermore, confidential interviews conducted with 27 production workers across three departments revealed a persistent pattern of verbal abuse, specifically public humiliation and the use of derogatory language by supervisory personnel to enforce production targets. Six separate worker accounts, corroborated across sewing, finishing, and packing sections, described incidents occurring as recently as the week prior to the audit, with no evidence of functional reporting or remediation through the newly established grievance committee, whose members stated they had received no case management training.
**Conclusion:** The factory has failed to effectively implement its CAP, demonstrating non-compliance with the established standard. The verified presence of abusive conduct, coupled with the incomplete rollout of corrective training and the non-functioning state of the grievance mechanism, constitutes an active and unresolved violation.
**Severity: Moderate**

[Contracts & Human Resources]
**Audit Finding Ref: HR-056-03-2024 (Contracts & Human Resources)**

During the review of human resources documentation and worker interviews conducted on March 12-14, 2024, it was found that the factory's implementation of compliant employment contracts remains inconsistent and fails to meet the standards outlined in the corrective action plan (CAP Ref: FAC-056-CAP-2023-11, Item 7). Background checks confirmed that of the 237 production workers on the payroll, only 189 had signed the updated, legally compliant contracts in the local language. Interviews with a sample of 15 workers from the finishing and cutting departments revealed that 7 individuals, all hired within the last four months, were still in possession of only their initial job offer letters, which lacked critical clauses on wages, working hours, and termination procedures. This represents a failure to rectify a previously identified systemic issue and leaves a significant portion of the workforce without formalized terms of employment, creating substantial legal and ethical risk. **Severity: Moderate.**

[Occupational Safety & Health]
**Audit Finding Reference:** OSH-2024-056-003
**Background & Context:** Factory 056 remains under a Corrective Action Plan (CAP Ref: Q4-2023-12) following significant occupational safety and health non-compliances identified during the previous surveillance audit. The current assessment, conducted on April 22-23, 2024, included a physical inspection of all production floors, storage areas, and maintenance rooms, alongside confidential interviews with 14 operators from different departments.
**Observations & Evidence:** During the walk-through, the audit team observed a recurring and systemic failure to maintain clear and unobstructed egress pathways. Specifically, in the cutting and finishing sections (noted on Floor 2), primary and secondary aisles were partially blocked by WIP (work-in-progress) trolleys and bales of raw material, creating consistent pinch points and impeding what would constitute a clear width for emergency evacuation. This was corroborated during worker interviews, where three separate operators from the cutting section expressed concerns about "having to squeeze past rolls of fabric" to access their workstations and the fire exits. This condition was immediately pointed out to factory management on-site and is a repeat violation from the previous CAP.
**Follow-up & Conclusion:** Despite prior commitments to implement a 5S program for housekeeping and aisle marking, the implementation remains inadequate and ineffective. This constitutes a failure to uphold section 7.8 of the Brand's Code of Conduct and represents an ongoing serious risk to worker safety in the event of an emergency requiring rapid egress.
**Severity: Moderate**


============================================================
Factory 057 - Audit Report
Factory Profile: factory recovering from recent fire incident, under special monitoring by local authorities
============================================================

[Freedom of Association & Collective Bargaining]
**Audit Finding Ref: FA-057-24-008 | Compliance Area: Freedom of Association & Collective Bargaining (Code: HR.04)**

Following the fire incident on March 15, 2024, which resulted in the temporary cessation of operations and subsequent special monitoring by the District Labor Office, this audit aimed to assess the current state of industrial relations and worker representation mechanisms. During the site inspection conducted on June 5-6, 2024, the auditor noted the absence of any visible postings regarding worker rights to association or minutes from collective bargaining meetings in common areas. Interviews with 17 production workers from various departments revealed a consistent narrative: while a Worker Welfare Committee had existed prior to the fire, its operations have been suspended indefinitely since the incident, and no new elections or meetings have been convened. Several workers expressed uncertainty about the committee's status and reported that management had verbally discouraged discussions about re-forming the committee, citing the factory's "fragile recovery period" as a reason to avoid "unnecessary disruptions." This constitutes a failure to maintain previously established channels for collective dialogue and raises concerns of interference with the right to freedom of association. **Severity: Moderate** A follow-up review with the local authorities is required to align the restoration of worker representation with the factory's rehabilitation plan.

[Harassment & Abuse]
**Audit Finding Ref: FA-057-24-HA-003 | Compliance Area: Harassment & Abuse (HA) | Audit Dates: October 22-24, 2024**

Following the disruption caused by the fire incident in Q3 2024 and the subsequent factory recovery under heightened supervision, the audit team sought to evaluate the stability of management systems and worker welfare in this period of operational stress. During worker interviews conducted on October 23, 2024, with 17 production line operators (approximately 12% of the shift), a recurring theme emerged regarding supervisory conduct on Line 7. Multiple workers, who requested anonymity citing fear of reprisal, described instances where the line supervisor, Mr. Chen, uses demeaning and threatening language to accelerate production, particularly during mandatory overtime shifts implemented to meet post-fire catch-up orders. One worker provided a specific account from October 18, where Mr. Chen loudly berated a worker for a sewing error, stating, "You are as useless as the burnt machinery; if you cannot work faster, you will be gone." This statement was corroborated in essence by two other interviewed workers from the same line. While the factory has a policy against harassment (SP-057-08), posted in the main canteen, interviews confirmed a widespread belief among workers on Line 7 that reporting such abuse through the designated channel would result in unfavorable shift assignments or dismissal, especially in the current climate of reduced orders. This constitutes a failure to effectively implement and communicate the policy and to provide a safe, confidential grievance mechanism, creating an environment of psychological coercion and verbal abuse. **Severity: Moderate.** A follow-up note is required to review the disciplinary action taken against the supervisor in question and the retraining provided to all line supervisors on the code of conduct and non-retaliation policies by November 30, 2024.

[Occupational Safety & Health]
**Audit Finding Ref:** OSH-057-08-2024
**Date of Inspection:** August 21-22, 2024
**Area:** Occupational Safety & Health - Emergency Preparedness and Fire Safety
**Background Context:** Given the factory’s status as a facility recovering from a significant fire incident (occurred April 2024) and currently under special monitoring by the local Fire Safety Bureau, particular emphasis was placed on evaluating the reinstatement and efficacy of fire prevention and emergency egress systems. Inspector observations on the first day identified that while primary production machinery had been largely restored, the reinstatement of complete passive fire protection measures was ongoing. During worker interviews conducted with 7 employees from the cutting and sewing sections on August 22, 4 confirmed they had not participated in a fire drill since the April incident, and 3 expressed uncertainty regarding the locations of newly installed secondary exits in the rebuilt western wing. Furthermore, a physical inspection revealed that 2 of the 5 newly mandated fire extinguishers (Type ABC, 10kg) in the finished goods warehouse, installed post-incident, had inspection tags indicating they were last serviced in December 2023, predating the fire, and were thus overdue for annual maintenance. This represents a failure to maintain critical safety equipment and ensure adequate employee preparedness, which is of heightened concern given the facility's recent history. **Follow-up Note:** The local authorities' monitoring report from July 2024 (Ref: LFB-057/07) had previously flagged the need for documented drill schedules.
**Severity: Moderate**

Factory 058 - Audit Report
Factory Profile: well-established factory with strong compliance history, ISO certified, dedicated compliance officer
============================================================

[Occupational Safety & Health]
**Audit Area:** 5.0 Occupational Safety & Health
**Reference:** OSH-2023-058-F07
**Date of Inspection:** October 26, 2023

A review of the factory's documented Safety & Health management system, which is integrated into its ISO 9001:2015 framework, indicates a robust procedural foundation and a commendable historical performance in this compliance area. During the physical inspection of the cutting department on the aforementioned date, the auditor observed that three of the five band knife machines (Asset IDs BK-12, BK-14, BK-17) were operational but lacked the required fixed physical guarding to prevent contact with the blade mechanism from the rear and sides, a condition corroborated during separate interviews with two cutting operators. While the factory’s compliance officer promptly initiated a work order to address the issue upon notification, and worker interviews confirmed regular safety training sessions are conducted, the absence of this primary safeguarding on multiple pieces of high-risk equipment constitutes a failure to implement a critical element of the factory's own documented Lockout/Tagout and Machine Safety procedures (Ref: FAC-PRO-OSH-004, Rev. 3). **Severity: Moderate.** A follow-up verification of corrective action, including photographic evidence of reinstalled guards, is required within 30 days.

[Freedom of Association & Collective Bargaining]
**Audit Finding Ref: FO-24-058-003**
**Compliance Area: Freedom of Association & Collective Bargaining (FA-CB)**
**Date of Discovery: October 26, 2023**

During a review of factory policies and subsequent confidential worker interviews conducted on October 25-26, 2023, with a stratified sample of 32 production workers from various departments, the audit team identified a procedural inconsistency in the facility's otherwise robust framework for industrial relations. While the factory maintains a democratically elected Worker Welfare Committee (WWC) that is recognized in the Employee Handbook (Rev. 7, Section 4.2), and management demonstrated a generally cooperative attitude during committee meetings as documented in minutes from the past quarter, investigator observations and worker testimony revealed that 8 of the 14 interviewed WWC members were unaware of their explicit right to collectively bargain on wages and benefits, as distinct from their role in raising workplace grievances. This gap in understanding constitutes a failure to ensure all worker representatives are fully educated on the scope of their rights under FA-CB principles, potentially hindering the committee's effectiveness. The factory is required to provide enhanced, role-specific training to all WWC members on the principles and mechanisms of collective bargaining, with evidence of completion to be verified at the next follow-up inspection.
**Severity: Minor**

[Wages & Benefits]
**Audit Finding Ref: A-F-058-24-003 | Compliance Area: C.01 Wages & Benefits | Date of Discovery: 17 October 2023**

While the factory maintains robust systems for base wage calculation and timely payment, evidenced by payroll review for June-August 2023, a discrepancy was identified between piece-rate production targets and actual earned wages for a specific worker category. Inspector observations of sewing section efficiency data, cross-referenced with the wage records of 8 randomly selected sewing operators paid on a piece-rate basis, indicated that 3 operators (37.5% of the sample) failed to meet the exceptionally high daily production quota required to attain the legal minimum wage for two out of the three months reviewed. Worker interviews conducted on 17 October 2023, with notes recorded as WI-058-07 through WI-058-12, corroborated this, with two interviewees stating they occasionally received less than the minimum wage during complex style changes, despite working a full 8-hour shift. This constitutes a failure to guarantee the legal minimum wage as per national labor law, irrespective of the payment system. **Severity: Moderate.** The factory management is required to review and recalibrate all piece-rate quotas to ensure they are reasonably attainable and to conduct back-pay calculations for affected workers for the previous six months.

[Child Labor]
During the review of personnel files and the subsequent verification of payroll records for the month of March 2024, and cross-referenced against worker interview notes from April 10, 2024, the audit team identified a discrepancy concerning a single individual. Although the factory maintains a robust age verification procedure for the vast majority of its 1,200-strong workforce, documentation for one worker assigned to the finishing section (Employee ID #F058-7842) indicated a date of birth that would make the individual 17 years old at the time of hiring six months prior. This was confirmed through a review of the original national identification card presented at hiring. While the young worker was not engaged in hazardous duties and local law permits employment at age 17, the factory's own written code of conduct, aligned with the buyer's specific standard (Ref: CL-1.2), clearly stipulates a minimum hiring age of 18. This represents a failure to fully implement the factory's own declared policy. The compliance officer was immediately notified and the worker has been reassigned to a non-production training role pending a formal review of this procedural lapse. **Severity: Minor**

Factory 059 - Audit Report
Factory Profile: well-established factory with strong compliance history, ISO certified, dedicated compliance officer
============================================================

[Child Labor]
**Audit Finding Reference: CL-2023-059-F01**

**Compliance Area: Child Labor**

A review of the factory's established Human Resources management system, including the comprehensive recruitment procedure (SOP-HR-001 Rev. 4), which incorporates document verification and age-screening protocols, was conducted. During the on-site inspection on October 26, 2023, a spot-check of personnel files for 47 production workers hired within the last 12 months was performed, with all files containing valid, government-issued age documentation and signed declarations of compliance with the minimum age requirement of 18 for production roles. Furthermore, interviews held with a randomized selection of 12 workers from the sewing and finishing sections confirmed hiring practices consistent with the documented procedure, with no discrepancies or allegations of underage labor raised. The presence of a dedicated compliance officer and the maturity of the ISO-certified management systems provide robust preventative controls in this area. **Status: Compliant.**

[Freedom of Association & Collective Bargaining]
**Audit Reference:** FA-059-24-Q3, Section 7.1 (Industrial Relations)
**Date of Assessment:** October 26, 2023
**Background & Context:** Factory 059 maintains a formally recognized Workers’ Welfare Committee (WWC), elected in January 2023, which management cites as its primary mechanism for worker-management dialogue. The factory’s policies, as documented in the HR manual Rev. 4, explicitly state compliance with national law regarding freedom of association.

**Observations & Interviews:** A review of meeting minutes from the WWC for the period March-October 2023 shows a consistent agenda focused solely on welfare topics (canteen food, festival bonuses) with no recorded discussion of collective bargaining on wages or working conditions. Interviews conducted with 14 workers from various departments on the audit date revealed that 9 were unaware of their right to form or join a trade union of their own choosing, mistakenly believing the management-supported WWC was the only permitted representative body. Furthermore, 3 workers from the sewing section reported a prevailing sense of apprehension regarding potential management reprisal for initiating discussions on unionization, despite no overt prohibitive statements being posted.

**Finding:** While no active obstruction of union formation was evidenced, the factory has failed to ensure workers are proactively informed and assured of their rights under FOA principles, creating an environment that may inhibit the free exercise of collective bargaining rights. The current communication and training protocols are insufficient to dispel worker misconceptions and ensure a neutral understanding of associational options.

**Severity: Minor**
**Follow-up Required:** Implementation of a corrective action plan to include targeted training sessions for all workers on FOA rights, conducted by a third-party resource, and a revision of onboarding materials, to be verified at the next surveillance audit.

[Discrimination]
**Audit Finding Ref: DISC-2023-059-02**
**Compliance Area:** Employment Discrimination
**Context:** During the routine social compliance audit conducted on October 26, 2023, a review of hiring, promotion, and disciplinary practices was undertaken to assess adherence to the factory's non-discrimination policy and local labor law. Factory 059 maintains a generally robust compliance framework, as evidenced by its ISO certification and the presence of a dedicated compliance officer.

**Observations & Interviews:** Documentation review of promotion records from the last fiscal year indicated a pattern where all eight supervisory promotions within the sewing department were awarded to male employees, despite approximately 65% of the department's workforce being female. During confidential worker interviews, conducted with 32 employees across various departments, three female operators in the sewing section separately reported a perceived "glass ceiling" for line leader positions, with one stating, "They tell us women are better with fine stitching, but only men get chosen to be supervisors." The compliance officer confirmed awareness of the disparity but cited historical precedent and perceived continuity of management style as contributing factors.

**Analysis:** This constitutes a *de facto* discriminatory practice based on gender, creating an unequal pathway for career advancement for female employees, which contravenes both the factory’s own policy and fundamental International Labor Organization conventions. While no overt discriminatory language was found in written policies, the practical outcome demonstrates a systemic bias.

**Severity: Moderate**
**Follow-up Required:** The factory must develop and implement a corrective action plan with clear, measurable goals for ensuring gender equity in promotion processes, including unbiased candidate selection criteria and training for management, to be verified at the next surveillance audit.

[Emergency Preparedness]
**Audit Finding Reference:** EP-059-2023-04
**Compliance Area:** Emergency Preparedness (EP-5, EP-7, EP-12)
**Background & Observation:** During the site inspection conducted on October 26, 2023, the audit team, while acknowledging the factory's generally well-maintained physical infrastructure and documented emergency procedures, identified a procedural lapse during the unannounced live fire drill for the Cutting and Sewing Department on the third floor. The drill, initiated at 14:15, revealed a failure to account for all personnel at the designated assembly point within the stipulated time. Subsequent review of the muster log and worker interviews indicated a 4-minute and 45-second delay in the full evacuation of the section, primarily attributed to the assigned floor warden for Section C being unaware of their responsibility due to a recent shift rotation, a detail not updated in the wardens' list dated Q3 2023. Interviews with 7 workers from that section confirmed the lack of clear instruction during the event.
**Analysis & Follow-up:** This constitutes a failure in the execution of the emergency preparedness plan, specifically regarding role clarity and communication, which could lead to injury in a real emergency. The factory's compliance officer has been tasked with reviewing and validating all warden assignments and conducting a refresher training session, with evidence due for review by November 30, 2023.
**Severity: Minor**

[Forced Labor]
During a review of recruitment practices for migrant workers, which was conducted as part of the broader forced labor assessment, it was identified that a subset of 37 workers hired between March and May 2024 through an external labor agency had been charged recruitment fees. Interviews conducted on 15 October 2024 with five affected workers from this group confirmed that fees ranging from 1,200 to 1,800 RMB were paid to the agency for their placement, a cost which was subsequently deducted from their first two months' wages at the factory. While management demonstrated awareness of the Client's Code of Conduct and provided signed agreements with the agency prohibiting such fees, the factory failed to implement adequate due diligence and reimbursement procedures to ensure compliance, thereby creating a debt burden for workers. This constitutes a violation of requirement FL-03 (Recruitment Fees) and licensee standard FL.01.01. Severity: Moderate. Corrective action requires the factory to conduct a full review, reimburse all affected workers with verifiable proof, and amend contractor agreements with enforceable penalties.


============================================================
Factory 060 - Audit Report
Factory Profile: newly established factory with 100-200 workers, young workforce, still building compliance systems
============================================================

[Wages & Benefits]
**Audit Finding Ref: 060-WB-02 | Compliance Area: Wages & Benefits | Date of Discovery: October 26, 2023**

During the review of payroll records for the period covering September 1-30, 2023, and corroborated through confidential interviews with 12 production workers selected at random, it was identified that the factory is not correctly compensating workers for overtime hours. Inspector observations of time cards and pay slips indicate a consistent pattern of paying the standard hourly rate for all hours worked, without applying the legally mandated overtime premium for hours exceeding the regular schedule. This was confirmed in worker interviews, with one operator noting, "We worked until 8 PM for ten days last month to finish the urgent order, but our pay slip only shows our normal rate." The factory's recently implemented payroll system lacks the configuration to automatically calculate the differential overtime rate, and management demonstrated a lack of awareness of this specific legal requirement. A review of the factory's wage policy documentation also omitted this provision. **Severity: Moderate** - A systemic failure resulting in underpayment, requiring immediate correction and retroactive remediation.

[Forced Labor]
**Audit Finding Ref: FL-06-024**
**Compliance Area: Forced Labor & Involuntary Employment (SA8000 Element 2, ILO Convention 29)**
**Date of Inspection: 2023-11-17**

During the review of payroll records for the period covering September and October 2023, and subsequent worker interviews, it was identified that the factory's practice regarding the retention of original identity documents presents a significant risk of coercion. The audit team, through physical verification, confirmed that the management holds the original national ID cards of 47 production operators, ostensibly for "safekeeping and administrative processing," as stated by the HR officer. In confidential interviews conducted on 2023-11-17 with 12 randomly selected workers from the sewing section, 3 workers expressed apprehension about requesting the return of their documents, fearing it would jeopardize their employment in this nascent facility. While no direct evidence of physical confinement or bonded labor was observed, the unilateral withholding of personal identity documents restricts workers’ freedom of movement and creates an inherent power imbalance, which is a recognized indicator of forced labor according to the ILO's guidelines. This is particularly concerning given the young demographic profile of the workforce, who may be less aware of their rights.
**Severity: Moderate**
**Follow-up Note:** Corrective Action Plan (CAP) must include the immediate, unconditional return of all original personal documents to workers, the implementation of a documented policy prohibiting this practice, and verified worker training on this policy by 2023-12-20.

[Emergency Preparedness]
**Audit Finding Reference:** EP-2023-060-02  
**Compliance Area:** Emergency Preparedness  
**Date of Inspection:** October 26, 2023  
**Background & Observations:** During the walkthrough of the facility, which is a newly established operation with an estimated 150 workers, it was noted that while primary exit routes are generally unobstructed, the factory's emergency preparedness systems are underdeveloped and inconsistent. Specifically, the documented emergency evacuation plan, requested for review, was a generic template not site-specific to the layout of Factory 060, lacking designated assembly areas and key personnel responsibilities. Furthermore, during functional testing, the alarm system in the western cutting section was found to be inaudible, registering at 65 dB against a required 85 dB at the furthest workstations, as measured by the inspector's sound level meter on the aforementioned date.  
**Worker Interviews:** Interviews conducted with 7 production workers from different departments on October 26 revealed that only 2 had participated in a full facility evacuation drill within the last 12 months; the majority reported participating only in sporadic, departmental "fire bell tests" with no subsequent briefing or drill evaluation. Several younger workers in the packing section expressed uncertainty about the location of their secondary exit.  
**Conclusion & Follow-up:** The absence of a site-specific plan, coupled with an inadequate alarm system and insufficient drill implementation, fails to ensure all workers can be reliably alerted and evacuated in an emergency. This represents a significant failure in establishing a foundational safety protocol for the young workforce. The factory management is required to submit a corrective action plan addressing these systemic gaps.  
**Severity: Moderate**

[Discrimination]
**Audit Reference:** SOC-060-24-003 | **Compliance Area:** 5.2 Non-Discrimination & Harassment | **Date of Assessment:** October 26, 2023

Following a review of the facility's nascent human resources policies and conducting confidential interviews on the shop floor, the audit team identified systemic gaps in the formalization and implementation of non-discrimination practices. While the factory’s stated hiring policy, as presented in draft documentation, professes commitment to equal opportunity, investigator observations and worker testimony indicate a de facto hiring preference for female workers in sewing operations and male workers in cutting and maintenance roles, with no objective criteria documented to justify this occupational segregation. Of the 18 workers interviewed across departments, 7 from the cutting section mentioned during discussions that they were unaware of any formal internal channel to report discriminatory treatment, and the factory management confirmed that specific training on non-discrimination has not yet been rolled out to the predominantly young workforce as their compliance systems are still under development. This constitutes a failure to establish and communicate clear procedures to prevent discrimination in employment, as required by the applicable code of conduct. **Severity: Moderate**

[Occupational Safety & Health]
**Audit Finding Reference:** SA-060-24-OSH-003
**Compliance Area:** Occupational Safety and Health (OSH)
**Date of Inspection:** 2024-10-26

**Background & Observations:** During the walkthrough of the cutting and sewing sections on 26 October 2024, it was noted that while the factory is new and the physical infrastructure appears modern, the implementation of a structured OSH program remains in its nascent stages. A review of documentation revealed the absence of a formally appointed and trained OSH officer, and no documented risk assessments or emergency drills have been conducted since operations commenced three months ago. Interviews with 7 production workers, selected at random, indicated a general lack of awareness of emergency evacuation procedures and the location of first-aid kits; one worker in the pressing area noted the fire extinguisher (ID #FE-C-12) was obstructed by a rolling rack of WIP garments. The management representative acknowledged the gaps, stating that systems are "still being built" and training is planned for Q1 of next year. However, the continued operation without these fundamental safety protocols in place exposes the young workforce to significant and uncontrolled risk.
**Severity: Critical**

[Child Labor]
During the document review conducted on 17 October 2023, the audit team noted that the factory's hiring procedures, while nascent, lacked a systematic age verification protocol as stipulated in code CL-01. Subsequent physical inspection of production areas on the same date revealed a workforce that appeared predominantly young, though no overtly young children were observed. Interviews with seven randomly selected workers from the cutting and sewing departments, however, uncovered that one individual, hired three months prior as a helper, admitted to being 16 years old but could not produce any original identification document to confirm this; the personnel file contained only a photocopy of what appeared to be a local student card. The factory management, when presented with this discrepancy, acknowledged the lapse in their vetting process, attributing it to the rapid onboarding of personnel during the start-up phase and an over-reliance on copies provided by a local labor contractor. Given the confirmed absence of a reliable age verification system and the identification discrepancy for a worker who may be under the legal working age, this constitutes a violation of the client's Code of Conduct and local labor law. Severity: Moderate. Corrective action requires immediate validation of the worker's age via original documents and the implementation of a robust age verification checklist for all hires, with evidence to be submitted within 30 days.

[Harassment & Abuse]
**Audit Finding Reference:** SA-060-24-008 | **Compliance Area:** Harassment & Abuse (COC Section 7.1) | **Date of Inspection:** 23 October 2024

**Background & Observations:** During the documentation review and facility walkthrough on 23 October 2024, it was noted that Factory 060, as a newly established operation with an estimated 150 workers primarily under 30 years of age, has not yet developed or implemented a formal policy or procedural framework to prevent harassment and abuse in the workplace. A review of posted materials and available employee handbooks found no reference to a code of conduct, grievance mechanism, or disciplinary measures related to harassment, abuse, or intimidation. Interviews were conducted with 17 workers across cutting, sewing, and finishing departments; of those interviewed, 14 confirmed they had never received any training or information on what constitutes unacceptable behavior or how to report concerns, with three workers from the sewing section anonymously describing an environment where "teasing and yelling by line leaders is common to meet targets" and where they "would not know who to tell if there was a serious problem." The absence of a defined policy and communicated procedure, coupled with worker testimony indicating occurrences of verbal abuse, demonstrates a systemic failure to provide a workplace free from harassment.
**Severity: Moderate**

**Follow-up Note:** Corrective Action Plan (CAP) must include the development of a written policy in the local language, establishment of a confidential reporting procedure, and implementation of mandatory manager and worker training by Q1 2025.

[Contracts & Human Resources]
**Audit Finding Ref: HR-04**  
**Compliance Area: Contracts & Human Records**  
**Date of Inspection: 23 October 2023**  

During the review of human resources documentation, it was observed that the factory, being newly established and still developing its administrative systems, has not yet implemented a standardized contract protocol for all employees. Of the 157 personnel files physically examined, only 68 contained signed employment contracts that clearly outlined terms of employment, wages, benefits, and termination procedures, representing approximately 43% coverage. Interviews conducted with a sample of 22 workers on the production floor on 23 October indicated that 15 had not received any written contract, while the remaining 7 confirmed receiving only a brief offer letter without detailed terms. This lack of systematic contracting exposes workers to potential ambiguities regarding their rights and obligations and fails to meet the requirement for providing clear, written terms of employment prior to work commencement. The management representative acknowledged this gap, citing the rapid onboarding of a young workforce and admitted the system is still under development. **Severity: Moderate**

[Freedom of Association & Collective Bargaining]
**Audit Reference: FOAB-060-24-008**  
**Compliance Area: Freedom of Association & Collective Bargaining (Section 8 of the CoC)**  

**Background & Observations:** During the site inspection conducted on 12 March 2024, the audit team reviewed the factory’s policies and noted that, due to the facility’s recent establishment (operational since Q3 2023), formal written procedures regarding freedom of association are still under development. While management verbally expressed openness to worker organization, no dedicated internal communication channels or documented processes for union formation or collective bargaining were observed. The team conducted confidential interviews with 28 production workers, selected across various departments and shifts.  

**Worker Interview Notes:** Multiple workers (9 of 28 interviewed) indicated uncertainty regarding their rights to associate, with one worker from the sewing section stating, “We have not been told if we can form a group, and we are afraid to ask because we are new here.” Another worker noted that while there is no union, workers sometimes raise issues informally through line leaders. However, there was no evidence of any elected worker representatives or collective bargaining agreements. Management confirmed that no requests for association have been received to date, but also acknowledged that no proactive training or awareness sessions on these rights have been conducted for the predominantly young workforce.  

**Finding:** The factory has failed to establish and communicate clear, formal procedures that guarantee workers’ rights to freedom of association and collective bargaining, as required by the Code of Conduct. Although no active suppression was evident, the lack of systematic communication, training, or designated mechanisms constitutes a failure to create an enabling environment for these rights, posing a risk of infringement as the workforce matures. A corrective action plan must be developed to implement a policy, conduct worker training, and establish a documented election process for worker representatives.  

**Severity: Moderate**

Factory 061 - Audit Report
Factory Profile: small family-owned factory with 50-100 workers, limited HR capacity, first time being audited
============================================================

[Working Hours & Overtime]
**Audit Finding Ref: WH-OT-2024-061-03**
**Compliance Area: Working Hours & Overtime (B.1)**
**Date of Discovery:** October 24, 2024

During the review of payroll records for the period of September 1-30, 2024, and corroborated through confidential interviews with 8 production line workers selected at random, it was established that the factory routinely exceeds the legal limit of 60 maximum working hours per week, including overtime. Inspector observations noted production schedules posted for the week of October 14-20 indicating seven consecutive working days. Worker interview notes revealed a consistent pattern of 12-hour shifts (07:00-19:00) with one-hour break, six and often seven days per week, to meet production deadlines, resulting in weekly hours ranging from 66 to 72. While management demonstrated a lack of formalized systems for tracking and authorizing overtime, attributed to limited HR capacity and being a first-time auditee, the absence of these controls does not mitigate the fundamental violation of maximum hour provisions. A follow-up note is required for the submission of a detailed corrective action plan addressing systematic recording, scheduling, and compliance with statutory limits.
**Severity: Critical**
