Factory 098 - Audit Report
Factory Profile: medium-sized factory with 200-400 workers, recently changed ownership, transitioning management
============================================================

[Wages & Benefits]
**Audit Finding Ref:** WB-098-04-2023
**Compliance Area:** Wages & Benefits
**Date of Discovery:** October 26, 2023

During the review of payroll records for September 2023 and worker interviews conducted on-site, a discrepancy was identified between the calculated wages and the amounts actually disbursed. Inspector observations confirmed that the factory’s payroll system, which is still being reconciled under the new ownership, failed to incorporate the legally mandated overtime premium for work performed on two national holidays in September, as attested by reviewed attendance sheets and production records. Interviews with 14 randomly selected production line workers from various departments confirmed unanimous testimony that their received pay for the pay period ending September 30 reflected only their standard hourly rate for those holiday hours, with no evidence of the legally required double-time compensation. This represents a failure to comply with statutory wage regulations and constitutes a non-payment of wages earned. The management representative acknowledged the systems gap during the closing meeting and attributed it to the ongoing transition, committing to a procedural review. **Severity: Moderate**

[Child Labor]
Review of payroll records for the period covering the last six months, alongside worker interviews conducted on October 26, 2023, revealed a discrepancy concerning one individual, payroll ID #098-47, hired under the previous ownership. This worker was listed as being 18 years of age at the time of hiring; however, cross-referencing the provided national ID card (serial number withheld) during the document verification process indicated a date of birth that would have made the individual 16 years old at the commencement of employment. While management stated they were unaware of this issue due to the ongoing transition and have since terminated the individual’s contract upon this discovery, the factory is in violation of CLS-01: Prohibition of Child Labor as defined by the applicable standard, as the individual was under the legal minimum age for employment during their period of work. A follow-up verification of the current workforce roster and age documentation is required. Severity: Moderate.


============================================================
Factory 099 - Audit Report
Factory Profile: well-established factory with strong compliance history, ISO certified, dedicated compliance officer
============================================================

[Forced Labor]
During our assessment on 17-18 October 2023, the audit team reviewed forced labor indicators as per SA8000:2014 and client code of conduct FL-01. While factory management maintains formal ISO-compliant policies and a worker grievance mechanism, interviews with 32 production line workers, conducted privately through an interpreter, revealed a recurring concern. Six workers from the stitching section, whose employment contracts and identification documents were reviewed and found to be in order, independently reported that their original government-issued identification cards (specifically National ID cards) were being retained by the line supervisors under a stated policy of "safe-keeping," with workers required to submit a formal request for their return, a process noted to often take 3-5 working days. This practice of withholding personal documents, even with a procedural return mechanism, constitutes a restriction of worker movement and freedom of employment, creating a potential condition of forced labor. The dedicated compliance officer was unaware of this localized departmental practice. **Severity: Moderate.** Corrective action requires the immediate cessation of this document retention practice and a management review of supervisory policies.

[Child Labor]
During the document review conducted on 23-24 October 2023, the auditor noted that the factory's hiring procedures, as outlined in its HR manual (CLP-099-01 Rev.7), require the submission of government-issued age verification for all candidates. However, a sample review of 35 personnel files from hires made in Q3 2023 revealed a single file, for worker ID #099-8472, where the provided national ID card appeared potentially non-genuine, exhibiting inconsistencies in print quality and hologram details when compared to verified samples. A subsequent confidential interview with the individual in question, conducted on 24 October, revealed the worker was unable to accurately recall key personal details listed on the submitted document and later admitted to being 17 years of age at the time of hiring, one year below the local legal minimum age of 18 for factory work. While management demonstrated immediate corrective action by suspending the worker with pay and initiating a formal investigation into the hiring lapse, this constitutes a failure in the recruitment verification process. **Severity: Moderate**

[Harassment & Abuse]
**Compliance Area:** 4.0 Harassment & Abuse (Ref: SA8000:2014 Sec 4.1 / BSCI Code para. 7)
**Finding Reference:** FA099-2023-081

A review of the factory's social management system documentation, including its detailed policy on harassment, abuse, and disciplinary practices, confirmed a robust written framework aligned with international standards. The presence of a dedicated Compliance Officer, Ms. Zhang Wei, and records of annual training sessions conducted on 15 March 2023 and 12 July 2023 for all managerial staff were noted. However, during confidential worker interviews conducted on 23 October 2023 with 32 randomly selected production operators from the sewing and finishing departments, three separate workers described an environment of verbal abuse and intimidation by one specific line supervisor (Supervisor ID: SL-22). These accounts, while not alleging physical abuse, consistently cited the use of demeaning language, public shouting, and threats of punitive work assignments or dismissal for minor performance errors, creating a climate of fear. The factory's established grievance mechanism, while physically accessible, was perceived by these interviewees as ineffective in this case due to fears of retaliation, indicating a breakdown between policy and implementation at the supervisory level. **Severity: Moderate** A corrective action plan is required to address this supervisory conduct and reinforce the non-retaliation policy through targeted training and confidential follow-up with the affected team.

[Discrimination]
**Audit Finding Ref: DF-2023-099-07 | Compliance Area: C.4 - Non-Discrimination | Date of Finding: October 26, 2023**

While a review of the factory's HR policies demonstrates a comprehensive non-discrimination clause aligned with international standards and local law, and the presence of a dedicated compliance officer is a noted strength, routine document examination and confidential worker interviews revealed a procedural inconsistency potentially leading to discriminatory outcomes. Specifically, during the review of hiring records for the past twelve months, it was observed that of 127 production operator hires, only 11 (approximately 8.7%) were female, despite a noted availability of qualified female applicants in the local labor market. In follow-up interviews conducted on October 25th with 4 female applicants who were not selected, 3 reported being asked during their interview about their marital status and future family plans, questions which were not posed to male applicants according to concurrent interviews with 5 newly hired male workers. This disparity in pre-employment questioning creates a risk of gender-based hiring bias, contravening section 4.2 of the factory's own code of conduct. The management has been advised to implement standardized, job-related interview questionnaires and provide refresher training to all hiring personnel. **Severity: Minor**

[Working Hours & Overtime]
**Compliance Area:** Working Hours & Overtime (WHOT)
**Audit Reference:** WHOT-099-2024-03-F1

**Finding:** An extensive review of time and attendance records for the period of January 1, 2024, through March 15, 2024, alongside payroll documentation, indicates a systemic failure to accurately compensate for all overtime hours worked. While the factory maintains a formal policy limiting work to 60 hours per week, inspector observations on March 12 and 13 noted a significant portion of the production workforce present beyond their scheduled shifts. Interviews conducted with 17 workers from the cutting and sewing departments revealed consistent testimony that, during peak production cycles, they were required to work until daily production targets were met, resulting in unrecorded overtime. Cross-referencing of worker testimonies with the provided electronic clock-in/out data for February shows a pattern of clock-outs being systematically aligned with the scheduled shift end, failing to capture the extended hours verbally reported by employees. This discrepancy constitutes a violation of local labor law and the applicable code of conduct regarding accurate payment for all hours worked. The factory's otherwise strong compliance history and management systems are noted, but the evidence indicates a procedural breakdown in recording and remunerating actual working time. **Severity: Moderate.** A corrective action plan must address the implementation of robust controls to ensure all working hours are captured and paid.


============================================================
Factory 100 - Audit Report
Factory Profile: subcontractor factory working for multiple brands, high production pressure, seasonal workforce
============================================================

[Occupational Safety & Health]
**Audit Finding Reference:** OSH-2023-100-04F
**Compliance Area:** Occupational Safety & Health (Specifically, Machine Guarding & Emergency Egress)
**Date of Inspection:** October 26, 2023

During the walkthrough of the second-floor sewing section, the audit team noted a consistent failure to reinstall protective guarding mechanisms on a total of seven industrial overlock sewing machines following routine maintenance activities, as corroborated by maintenance logs from the prior week. This observation was compounded by the placement of finished goods racks and bundled fabric rolls partially obstructing the designated primary emergency exit route in the same work area, reducing the clear width of the passage to approximately 0.8 meters, which is below the minimum required standard. Interviews conducted with four operatives from the seasonal workforce on October 25 confirmed a general lack of recent machine safety training and unclear understanding of lockout-tagout procedures, with one worker stating, "We are told to keep working when the mechanics are done, even if the plastic cover is not back on." The factory management attributed these lapses to high production pressure and rapid turnover of temporary staff but acknowledged the deficiency. This presents a significant and immediate risk of severe laceration or amputation injury, coupled with compromised evacuation readiness in the event of a fire.
**Severity: Critical**
**Follow-up Required:** Immediate Corrective Action Plan requested within 48 hours, with photographic evidence of remediation to be submitted.

[Discrimination]
**Compliance Area: 3.1 Discrimination (Policy & Practices) – Audit Code: HR-07**

During the document review on 12 March 2024, the auditor noted the factory's written policy prohibiting discrimination, as required. However, subsequent observations on the production floor and interviews with a cross-section of 18 workers from various departments revealed systemic discrepancies in hiring and assignment practices. Multiple workers from the finishing and packing sections, interviewed on 13 March 2024, stated that supervisory staff routinely request "young ladies from the countryside" for sewing line positions during peak season, citing their perceived dexterity and compliance, while male applicants and older female workers are predominantly offered roles in cutting, loading, and maintenance. This pattern was corroborated by a review of recent hiring records (Ref: Staffing Log Q1-2024), which showed a 92% correlation between gender and department assignment for the 127 temporary workers hired in the last quarter. The policy is therefore not effectively implemented, documented, or communicated, leading to discriminatory placement that limits equal opportunity and access to higher-skilled positions. **Severity: Moderate**. Follow-up required: Management must provide evidence of revised hiring/placement procedures and supervisor training by Q2.
